  727. I switched from waxing to epilating my legs about a year ago and will never go back. Epilators make life a lot easier for us fuzzy folks -- we don't have to shave daily, don't have to deal with sticky home wax products, and don't have to spend time and money on professional waxing. I use the Philips HP6401 Satinelle Epilator and am very satisfied with it as a leg epilator, so I hoped the Emoji AP-9L would be equally effective for bikini-area hair management.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the Emjoi AP-9L has 2 significant, related design flaws. The area of the device beneath the pinchers is not well-sealed, and bits of hair get stuck inside the device. Customers are provided with a small brush for removing hair and that helps somewhat, but it seems like a certain amount of hair will always escape into the device, which, I suspect, could interfere with performance later on. Additionally, the angle of the pinchers seems not quite ideal for grabbing hair and I've noticed that it works better on hair that's quite a bit longer than my Philips requires. This means that the hair that gets stuck in the device amounts to more volume than necessary. (Note that all epilators require a minimum hair length [similar to waxing] but it seems that the Emjoi AP-9L's minimum length is longer than optimal.) Because of this longer-than-ideal minimum hair length, the Emjoi doesn't get an area as cleanly shaven as I've come to expect with my Philips. It's possible that after several full epilations, once hair has thinned out, the left-behind-hair will be less noticeable, although still long enough that I suspect tweezing would be in order, which would defeat the purpose of epilating.
